<s> and cos who took occasion majestically to inquire of grady what the mischief was and who was crying had for answer that twas a woman another of them and that they were in grady's opinion the cause of most all the mischief in the world <\s>
<s> in which pen begins to doubt about his election whilst pen in his own county was thus carrying on his selfish plans and parliamentary schemes news came to him that lady rockminster had arrived at baymouth and had brought with her our friend laura <\s>
<s> at the announcement that laura his sister was near him pen felt rather guilty <\s>
<s> his wish was to stand higher in her esteem perhaps than in that of any other person in the world <\s>
<s> she was his mother's legacy to him <\s>
<s> he was to be her patron and protector in some sort <\s>
<s> how would she brave the news which he had to tell her and how should he explain the plans which he was meditating <\s>
<s> he felt as if neither he nor blanche could bear laura's dazzling glance of calm scrutiny and as if he would not dare to disclose his worldly hopes and ambitions to that spotless judge <\s>
<s> at her arrival at baymouth he wrote a letter thither which contained a great number of fine phrases and protests of affection and a great deal of easy satire and raillery in the midst of all which mr <\s>
<s> pen could not help feeling that he was in panic and that he was acting like a rogue and hypocrite <\s>
<s> how was it that a simple country girl should be the object of fear and trembling to such an accomplished gentleman as mr <\s>
<s> his worldly tactics and diplomacy his satire and knowledge of the world could not bear the test of her purity he felt somehow <\s>
<s> and he had to own to himself that his affairs were in such a position that he could not tell the truth to that honest soul <\s>
<s> as he rode from clavering to baymouth he felt as guilty as a schoolboy who doesn't know his lesson and is about to face the awful master <\s>
<s> for is not truth the master always and does she not have the power and hold the book <\s>
<s> under the charge of her kind though somewhat wayward and absolute patroness lady rockminster laura had seen somewhat of the world in the last year had gathered some accomplishments and profited by the lessons of society <\s>
<s> many a girl who had been accustomed to that too great tenderness in which laura's early life had been passed would have been unfitted for the changed existence which she now had to lead <\s>
<s> helen worshipped her two children and thought as home bred women will that all the world was made for them or to be considered after them <\s>
<s> she tended laura with a watchfulness of affection which never left her <\s>
<s> if she had a headache the widow was as alarmed as if there had never been an aching head before in the world <\s>
<s> she slept and woke read and moved under her mother's fond superintendence which was now withdrawn from her along with the tender creature whose anxious heart would beat no more <\s>
<s> and painful moments of grief and depression no doubt laura had when she stood in the great careless world alone <\s>
<s> nobody heeded her griefs or her solitude <\s>
<s> she was not quite the equal in social rank of the lady whose companion she was or of the friends and relatives of the imperious but kind old dowager <\s>
<s> some very likely bore her no goodwill some perhaps slighted her it might have been that servants were occasionally rude their mistress certainly was often <\s>
<s> laura not seldom found herself in family meetings the confidence and familiarity of which she felt were interrupted by her intrusion and her sensitiveness of course was wounded at the idea that she should give or feel this annoyance <\s>
<s> how many governesses are there in the world thought cheerful laura how many ladies whose necessities make them slaves and companions by profession <\s>
<s> what bad tempers and coarse unkindness have not these to encounter <\s>
<s> how infinitely better my lot is with these really kind and affectionate people than that of thousands of unprotected girls <\s>
<s> it was with this cordial spirit that our young lady adapted herself to her new position and went in advance of her fortune with a trustful smile <\s>
<s> did you ever know a person who met fortune in that way whom the goddess did not regard kindly <\s>
<s> are not even bad people won by a constant cheerfulness and a pure and affectionate heart <\s>
<s> when the babes in the wood in the ballad looked up fondly and trustfully at those notorious rogues whom their uncle had set to make away with the little folks we all know how one of the rascals relented and made away with the other not having the heart to be unkind to so much innocence and beauty <\s>
<s> oh happy they who have that virgin loving trust and sweet smiling confidence in the world and fear no evil because they think none <\s>
<s> miss laura bell was one of these fortunate persons and besides the gentle widow's little cross which as we have seen pen gave her had such a sparkling and brilliant kohinoor in her bosom as is even more precious than that famous jewel for it not only fetches a price and is retained by its owner in another world where diamonds are stated to be of no value but here too is of inestimable worth to its possessor is a talisman against evil and lightens up the darkness of life like cogia hassan's famous stone <\s>
<s> so that before miss bell had been a year in lady rockminster's house there was not a single person in it whose love she had not won by the use of this talisman <\s>
<s> from the old lady to the lowest dependent of her bounty laura had secured the goodwill and kindness of everybody <\s>
<s> with a mistress of such a temper my lady's woman who had endured her mistress for forty years and had been clawed and scolded and jibed every day and night in that space of time could not be expected to have a good temper of her own and was at first angry against miss laura as she had been against her ladyship's fifteen preceding companions <\s>
<s> but when laura was ill at paris this old woman nursed her in spite of her mistress who was afraid of catching the fever and absolutely fought for her medicine with martha from fairoaks now advanced to be miss laura's own maid <\s>
<s> as she was recovering grandjean the chef wanted to kill her by the numbers of delicacies which he dressed for her and wept when she ate her first slice of chicken <\s>
<s> the swiss major domo of the house celebrated miss bell's praises in almost every european language which he spoke with indifferent incorrectness the coachman was happy to drive her out the page cried when he heard she was ill and calverley and coldstream those two footmen so large so calm ordinarily and so difficult to move broke out into extraordinary hilarity at the news of her convalescence and intoxicated the page at a wine shop to fete laura's recovery <\s>
<s> even lady diana pynsent our former acquaintance mr <\s>
<s> pynsent had married by this time lady diana who had had a considerable dislike to laura for some time was so enthusiastic as to say that she thought miss bell was a very agreeable person and that grandmamma had found a great trouvaille in her <\s>
<s> all this goodwill and kindness laura had acquired not by any arts not by any flattery but by the simple force of good nature and by the blessed gift of pleasing and being pleased <\s>

<s> at her arrival at baymouth he wrote a letter thither which contained a great number of fine phrases and protests of affection and a great deal of easy satire and raillery in the midst of all which mr <\s>
<s> pen could not help feeling that he was in panic and that he was acting like a rogue and hypocrite <\s>
<s> how was it that a simple country girl should be the object of fear and trembling to such an accomplished gentleman as mr <\s>
<s> his worldly tactics and diplomacy his satire and knowledge of the world could not bear the test of her purity he felt somehow <\s>
<s> and he had to own to himself that his affairs were in such a position that he could not tell the truth to that honest soul <\s>
<s> as he rode from clavering to baymouth he felt as guilty as a schoolboy who doesn't know his lesson and is about to face the awful master <\s>
<s> for is not truth the master always and does she not have the power and hold the book <\s>
<s> under the charge of her kind though somewhat wayward and absolute patroness lady rockminster laura had seen somewhat of the world in the last year had gathered some accomplishments and profited by the lessons of society <\s>
<s> many a girl who had been accustomed to that too great tenderness in which laura's early life had been passed would have been unfitted for the changed existence which she now had to lead <\s>
<s> helen worshipped her two children and thought as home bred women will that all the world was made for them or to be considered after them <\s>
<s> she tended laura with a watchfulness of affection which never left her <\s>
<s> if she had a headache the widow was as alarmed as if there had never been an aching head before in the world <\s>
<s> she slept and woke read and moved under her mother's fond superintendence which was now withdrawn from her along with the tender creature whose anxious heart would beat no more <\s>
<s> and painful moments of grief and depression no doubt laura had when she stood in the great careless world alone <\s>
<s> nobody heeded her griefs or her solitude <\s>
<s> she was not quite the equal in social rank of the lady whose companion she was or of the friends and relatives of the imperious but kind old dowager <\s>
<s> some very likely bore her no goodwill some perhaps slighted her it might have been that servants were occasionally rude their mistress certainly was often <\s>
<s> laura not seldom found herself in family meetings the confidence and familiarity of which she felt were interrupted by her intrusion and her sensitiveness of course was wounded at the idea that she should give or feel this annoyance <\s>
<s> how many governesses are there in the world thought cheerful laura how many ladies whose necessities make them slaves and companions by profession <\s>
<s> what bad tempers and coarse unkindness have not these to encounter <\s>
<s> how infinitely better my lot is with these really kind and affectionate people than that of thousands of unprotected girls <\s>

<s> did you ever know a person who met fortune in that way whom the goddess did not regard kindly <\s>
<s> are not even bad people won by a constant cheerfulness and a pure and affectionate heart <\s>
<s> when the babes in the wood in the ballad looked up fondly and trustfully at those notorious rogues whom their uncle had set to make away with the little folks we all know how one of the rascals relented and made away with the other not having the heart to be unkind to so much innocence and beauty <\s>
<s> oh happy they who have that virgin loving trust and sweet smiling confidence in the world and fear no evil because they think none <\s>
<s> miss laura bell was one of these fortunate persons and besides the gentle widow's little cross which as we have seen pen gave her had such a sparkling and brilliant kohinoor in her bosom as is even more precious than that famous jewel for it not only fetches a price and is retained by its owner in another world where diamonds are stated to be of no value but here too is of inestimable worth to its possessor is a talisman against evil and lightens up the darkness of life like cogia hassan's famous stone <\s>
<s> so that before miss bell had been a year in lady rockminster's house there was not a single person in it whose love she had not won by the use of this talisman <\s>
<s> from the old lady to the lowest dependent of her bounty laura had secured the goodwill and kindness of everybody <\s>
<s> with a mistress of such a temper my lady's woman who had endured her mistress for forty years and had been clawed and scolded and jibed every day and night in that space of time could not be expected to have a good temper of her own and was at first angry against miss laura as she had been against her ladyship's fifteen preceding companions <\s>
<s> but when laura was ill at paris this old woman nursed her in spite of her mistress who was afraid of catching the fever and absolutely fought for her medicine with martha from fairoaks now advanced to be miss laura's own maid <\s>
<s> as she was recovering grandjean the chef wanted to kill her by the numbers of delicacies which he dressed for her and wept when she ate her first slice of chicken <\s>
<s> the swiss major domo of the house celebrated miss bell's praises in almost every european language which he spoke with indifferent incorrectness the coachman was happy to drive her out the page cried when he heard she was ill and calverley and coldstream those two footmen so large so calm ordinarily and so difficult to move broke out into extraordinary hilarity at the news of her convalescence and intoxicated the page at a wine shop to fete laura's recovery <\s>
<s> even lady diana pynsent our former acquaintance mr <\s>
<s> pynsent had married by this time lady diana who had had a considerable dislike to laura for some time was so enthusiastic as to say that she thought miss bell was a very agreeable person and that grandmamma had found a great trouvaille in her <\s>
<s> all this goodwill and kindness laura had acquired not by any arts not by any flattery but by the simple force of good nature and by the blessed gift of pleasing and being pleased <\s>
<s> on the one or two occasions when he had seen lady rockminster the old lady who did not admire him had been very pitiless and abrupt with our young friend and perhaps pen expected when he came to baymouth to find laura installed in her house in the quality of humble companion and treated no better than himself <\s>
<s> when she heard of his arrival she came running downstairs and i am not sure that she did not embrace him in the presence of calverley and coldstream not that those gentlemen ever told if the fractus orbis had come to a smash if laura instead of kissing pen had taken her scissors and snipped off his head calverley and coldstream would have looked on impavidly without allowing a grain of powder to be disturbed by the calamity <\s>
<s> laura had so much improved in health and looks that pen could not but admire her <\s>
<s> the frank and kind eyes which met his beamed with good health the cheek which he kissed blushed with beauty <\s>
<s> as he looked at her artless and graceful pure and candid he thought he had never seen her so beautiful <\s>
<s> why should he remark her beauty now so much and remark too to himself that he had not remarked it sooner <\s>

<s> he was affected and touched by the tender tone and the pure sparkling glance their innocence smote him somehow and moved him <\s>

<s> as she was recovering grandjean the chef wanted to kill her by the numbers of delicacies which he dressed for her and wept when she ate her first slice of chicken <\s>
<s> the swiss major domo of the house celebrated miss bell's praises in almost every european language which he spoke with indifferent incorrectness the coachman was happy to drive her out the page cried when he heard she was ill and calverley and coldstream those two footmen so large so calm ordinarily and so difficult to move broke out into extraordinary hilarity at the news of her convalescence and intoxicated the page at a wine shop to fete laura's recovery <\s>
<s> even lady diana pynsent our former acquaintance mr <\s>
<s> pynsent had married by this time lady diana who had had a considerable dislike to laura for some time was so enthusiastic as to say that she thought miss bell was a very agreeable person and that grandmamma had found a great trouvaille in her <\s>
<s> all this goodwill and kindness laura had acquired not by any arts not by any flattery but by the simple force of good nature and by the blessed gift of pleasing and being pleased <\s>
<s> on the one or two occasions when he had seen lady rockminster the old lady who did not admire him had been very pitiless and abrupt with our young friend and perhaps pen expected when he came to baymouth to find laura installed in her house in the quality of humble companion and treated no better than himself <\s>
<s> when she heard of his arrival she came running downstairs and i am not sure that she did not embrace him in the presence of calverley and coldstream not that those gentlemen ever told if the fractus orbis had come to a smash if laura instead of kissing pen had taken her scissors and snipped off his head calverley and coldstream would have looked on impavidly without allowing a grain of powder to be disturbed by the calamity <\s>
<s> laura had so much improved in health and looks that pen could not but admire her <\s>
<s> the frank and kind eyes which met his beamed with good health the cheek which he kissed blushed with beauty <\s>
<s> as he looked at her artless and graceful pure and candid he thought he had never seen her so beautiful <\s>
<s> why should he remark her beauty now so much and remark too to himself that he had not remarked it sooner <\s>
<s> he took her fair trustful hand and kissed it fondly he looked in her bright clear eyes and read in them that kindling welcome which he was always sure to find there <\s>
<s> he was affected and touched by the tender tone and the pure sparkling glance their innocence smote him somehow and moved him <\s>
<s> how good you are to me laura sister <\s>
<s> said pen i don't deserve that you should that you should be so kind to me <\s>

<s> betsy or blanche looked quite bewildered and began to scream too once twice thrice and it was her piercing shrieks which captain costigan heard as he walked the court below <\s>
<s> at the sound of these shrieks the perplexed parent clasped his hands his wristbands were open and on one brawny arm you could see letters tattooed in blue and rushing to his apartment came back with an eau de cologne bottle from his grand silver dressing case with the fragrant contents of which he began liberally to sprinkle bonner and blanche <\s>

<s> and cos who took occasion majestically to inquire of grady what the mischief was and who was crying had for answer that twas a woman another of them and that they were in grady's opinion the cause of most all the mischief in the world <\s>
<s> in which pen begins to doubt about his election whilst pen in his own county was thus carrying on his selfish plans and parliamentary schemes news came to him that lady rockminster had arrived at baymouth and had brought with her our friend laura <\s>
<s> at the announcement that laura his sister was near him pen felt rather guilty <\s>
<s> his wish was to stand higher in her esteem perhaps than in that of any other person in the world <\s>
<s> she was his mother's legacy to him <\s>
<s> he was to be her patron and protector in some sort <\s>
<s> how would she brave the news which he had to tell her and how should he explain the plans which he was meditating <\s>
<s> he felt as if neither he nor blanche could bear laura's dazzling glance of calm scrutiny and as if he would not dare to disclose his worldly hopes and ambitions to that spotless judge <\s>
<s> at her arrival at baymouth he wrote a letter thither which contained a great number of fine phrases and protests of affection and a great deal of easy satire and raillery in the midst of all which mr <\s>
<s> pen could not help feeling that he was in panic and that he was acting like a rogue and hypocrite <\s>
<s> how was it that a simple country girl should be the object of fear and trembling to such an accomplished gentleman as mr <\s>
<s> his worldly tactics and diplomacy his satire and knowledge of the world could not bear the test of her purity he felt somehow <\s>
<s> and he had to own to himself that his affairs were in such a position that he could not tell the truth to that honest soul <\s>
<s> as he rode from clavering to baymouth he felt as guilty as a schoolboy who doesn't know his lesson and is about to face the awful master <\s>
<s> for is not truth the master always and does she not have the power and hold the book <\s>
<s> under the charge of her kind though somewhat wayward and absolute patroness lady rockminster laura had seen somewhat of the world in the last year had gathered some accomplishments and profited by the lessons of society <\s>
<s> many a girl who had been accustomed to that too great tenderness in which laura's early life had been passed would have been unfitted for the changed existence which she now had to lead <\s>
<s> helen worshipped her two children and thought as home bred women will that all the world was made for them or to be considered after them <\s>
<s> she tended laura with a watchfulness of affection which never left her <\s>
<s> if she had a headache the widow was as alarmed as if there had never been an aching head before in the world <\s>
<s> she slept and woke read and moved under her mother's fond superintendence which was now withdrawn from her along with the tender creature whose anxious heart would beat no more <\s>
<s> and painful moments of grief and depression no doubt laura had when she stood in the great careless world alone <\s>
<s> nobody heeded her griefs or her solitude <\s>
<s> she was not quite the equal in social rank of the lady whose companion she was or of the friends and relatives of the imperious but kind old dowager <\s>
<s> some very likely bore her no goodwill some perhaps slighted her it might have been that servants were occasionally rude their mistress certainly was often <\s>
<s> laura not seldom found herself in family meetings the confidence and familiarity of which she felt were interrupted by her intrusion and her sensitiveness of course was wounded at the idea that she should give or feel this annoyance <\s>

<s> oh happy they who have that virgin loving trust and sweet smiling confidence in the world and fear no evil because they think none <\s>

<s> in which pen begins to doubt about his election whilst pen in his own county was thus carrying on his selfish plans and parliamentary schemes news came to him that lady rockminster had arrived at baymouth and had brought with her our friend laura <\s>
<s> at the announcement that laura his sister was near him pen felt rather guilty <\s>
<s> his wish was to stand higher in her esteem perhaps than in that of any other person in the world <\s>
<s> she was his mother's legacy to him <\s>
<s> he was to be her patron and protector in some sort <\s>
<s> how would she brave the news which he had to tell her and how should he explain the plans which he was meditating <\s>
<s> he felt as if neither he nor blanche could bear laura's dazzling glance of calm scrutiny and as if he would not dare to disclose his worldly hopes and ambitions to that spotless judge <\s>
<s> at her arrival at baymouth he wrote a letter thither which contained a great number of fine phrases and protests of affection and a great deal of easy satire and raillery in the midst of all which mr <\s>
<s> pen could not help feeling that he was in panic and that he was acting like a rogue and hypocrite <\s>
<s> how was it that a simple country girl should be the object of fear and trembling to such an accomplished gentleman as mr <\s>
<s> his worldly tactics and diplomacy his satire and knowledge of the world could not bear the test of her purity he felt somehow <\s>
<s> and he had to own to himself that his affairs were in such a position that he could not tell the truth to that honest soul <\s>
<s> as he rode from clavering to baymouth he felt as guilty as a schoolboy who doesn't know his lesson and is about to face the awful master <\s>
<s> for is not truth the master always and does she not have the power and hold the book <\s>
<s> under the charge of her kind though somewhat wayward and absolute patroness lady rockminster laura had seen somewhat of the world in the last year had gathered some accomplishments and profited by the lessons of society <\s>
<s> many a girl who had been accustomed to that too great tenderness in which laura's early life had been passed would have been unfitted for the changed existence which she now had to lead <\s>
<s> helen worshipped her two children and thought as home bred women will that all the world was made for them or to be considered after them <\s>
<s> she tended laura with a watchfulness of affection which never left her <\s>
<s> if she had a headache the widow was as alarmed as if there had never been an aching head before in the world <\s>
<s> she slept and woke read and moved under her mother's fond superintendence which was now withdrawn from her along with the tender creature whose anxious heart would beat no more <\s>
<s> and painful moments of grief and depression no doubt laura had when she stood in the great careless world alone <\s>
<s> nobody heeded her griefs or her solitude <\s>
<s> she was not quite the equal in social rank of the lady whose companion she was or of the friends and relatives of the imperious but kind old dowager <\s>
<s> some very likely bore her no goodwill some perhaps slighted her it might have been that servants were occasionally rude their mistress certainly was often <\s>
<s> laura not seldom found herself in family meetings the confidence and familiarity of which she felt were interrupted by her intrusion and her sensitiveness of course was wounded at the idea that she should give or feel this annoyance <\s>
<s> how many governesses are there in the world thought cheerful laura how many ladies whose necessities make them slaves and companions by profession <\s>
<s> what bad tempers and coarse unkindness have not these to encounter <\s>
<s> how infinitely better my lot is with these really kind and affectionate people than that of thousands of unprotected girls <\s>
<s> it was with this cordial spirit that our young lady adapted herself to her new position and went in advance of her fortune with a trustful smile <\s>
<s> did you ever know a person who met fortune in that way whom the goddess did not regard kindly <\s>
<s> are not even bad people won by a constant cheerfulness and a pure and affectionate heart <\s>
<s> when the babes in the wood in the ballad looked up fondly and trustfully at those notorious rogues whom their uncle had set to make away with the little folks we all know how one of the rascals relented and made away with the other not having the heart to be unkind to so much innocence and beauty <\s>
<s> oh happy they who have that virgin loving trust and sweet smiling confidence in the world and fear no evil because they think none <\s>
<s> miss laura bell was one of these fortunate persons and besides the gentle widow's little cross which as we have seen pen gave her had such a sparkling and brilliant kohinoor in her bosom as is even more precious than that famous jewel for it not only fetches a price and is retained by its owner in another world where diamonds are stated to be of no value but here too is of inestimable worth to its possessor is a talisman against evil and lightens up the darkness of life like cogia hassan's famous stone <\s>
<s> so that before miss bell had been a year in lady rockminster's house there was not a single person in it whose love she had not won by the use of this talisman <\s>
<s> from the old lady to the lowest dependent of her bounty laura had secured the goodwill and kindness of everybody <\s>
<s> with a mistress of such a temper my lady's woman who had endured her mistress for forty years and had been clawed and scolded and jibed every day and night in that space of time could not be expected to have a good temper of her own and was at first angry against miss laura as she had been against her ladyship's fifteen preceding companions <\s>
<s> but when laura was ill at paris this old woman nursed her in spite of her mistress who was afraid of catching the fever and absolutely fought for her medicine with martha from fairoaks now advanced to be miss laura's own maid <\s>
<s> as she was recovering grandjean the chef wanted to kill her by the numbers of delicacies which he dressed for her and wept when she ate her first slice of chicken <\s>
<s> the swiss major domo of the house celebrated miss bell's praises in almost every european language which he spoke with indifferent incorrectness the coachman was happy to drive her out the page cried when he heard she was ill and calverley and coldstream those two footmen so large so calm ordinarily and so difficult to move broke out into extraordinary hilarity at the news of her convalescence and intoxicated the page at a wine shop to fete laura's recovery <\s>

<s> and painful moments of grief and depression no doubt laura had when she stood in the great careless world alone <\s>
<s> nobody heeded her griefs or her solitude <\s>
<s> she was not quite the equal in social rank of the lady whose companion she was or of the friends and relatives of the imperious but kind old dowager <\s>
<s> some very likely bore her no goodwill some perhaps slighted her it might have been that servants were occasionally rude their mistress certainly was often <\s>
<s> laura not seldom found herself in family meetings the confidence and familiarity of which she felt were interrupted by her intrusion and her sensitiveness of course was wounded at the idea that she should give or feel this annoyance <\s>
<s> how many governesses are there in the world thought cheerful laura how many ladies whose necessities make them slaves and companions by profession <\s>
<s> what bad tempers and coarse unkindness have not these to encounter <\s>
<s> how infinitely better my lot is with these really kind and affectionate people than that of thousands of unprotected girls <\s>

<s> did you ever know a person who met fortune in that way whom the goddess did not regard kindly <\s>
<s> are not even bad people won by a constant cheerfulness and a pure and affectionate heart <\s>

<s> oh happy they who have that virgin loving trust and sweet smiling confidence in the world and fear no evil because they think none <\s>
<s> miss laura bell was one of these fortunate persons and besides the gentle widow's little cross which as we have seen pen gave her had such a sparkling and brilliant kohinoor in her bosom as is even more precious than that famous jewel for it not only fetches a price and is retained by its owner in another world where diamonds are stated to be of no value but here too is of inestimable worth to its possessor is a talisman against evil and lightens up the darkness of life like cogia hassan's famous stone <\s>
<s> so that before miss bell had been a year in lady rockminster's house there was not a single person in it whose love she had not won by the use of this talisman <\s>
<s> from the old lady to the lowest dependent of her bounty laura had secured the goodwill and kindness of everybody <\s>
<s> with a mistress of such a temper my lady's woman who had endured her mistress for forty years and had been clawed and scolded and jibed every day and night in that space of time could not be expected to have a good temper of her own and was at first angry against miss laura as she had been against her ladyship's fifteen preceding companions <\s>
<s> but when laura was ill at paris this old woman nursed her in spite of her mistress who was afraid of catching the fever and absolutely fought for her medicine with martha from fairoaks now advanced to be miss laura's own maid <\s>

<s> the swiss major domo of the house celebrated miss bell's praises in almost every european language which he spoke with indifferent incorrectness the coachman was happy to drive her out the page cried when he heard she was ill and calverley and coldstream those two footmen so large so calm ordinarily and so difficult to move broke out into extraordinary hilarity at the news of her convalescence and intoxicated the page at a wine shop to fete laura's recovery <\s>

<s> pynsent had married by this time lady diana who had had a considerable dislike to laura for some time was so enthusiastic as to say that she thought miss bell was a very agreeable person and that grandmamma had found a great trouvaille in her <\s>
<s> all this goodwill and kindness laura had acquired not by any arts not by any flattery but by the simple force of good nature and by the blessed gift of pleasing and being pleased <\s>
<s> on the one or two occasions when he had seen lady rockminster the old lady who did not admire him had been very pitiless and abrupt with our young friend and perhaps pen expected when he came to baymouth to find laura installed in her house in the quality of humble companion and treated no better than himself <\s>

<s> laura had so much improved in health and looks that pen could not but admire her <\s>

<s> why should he remark her beauty now so much and remark too to himself that he had not remarked it sooner <\s>

<s> he was affected and touched by the tender tone and the pure sparkling glance their innocence smote him somehow and moved him <\s>

<s> in which pen begins to doubt about his election whilst pen in his own county was thus carrying on his selfish plans and parliamentary schemes news came to him that lady rockminster had arrived at baymouth and had brought with her our friend laura <\s>
<s> at the announcement that laura his sister was near him pen felt rather guilty <\s>

<s> as he looked at her artless and graceful pure and candid he thought he had never seen her so beautiful <\s>
<s> why should he remark her beauty now so much and remark too to himself that he had not remarked it sooner <\s>
<s> he took her fair trustful hand and kissed it fondly he looked in her bright clear eyes and read in them that kindling welcome which he was always sure to find there <\s>
<s> he was affected and touched by the tender tone and the pure sparkling glance their innocence smote him somehow and moved him <\s>

<s> betsy or blanche looked quite bewildered and began to scream too once twice thrice and it was her piercing shrieks which captain costigan heard as he walked the court below <\s>
<s> at the sound of these shrieks the perplexed parent clasped his hands his wristbands were open and on one brawny arm you could see letters tattooed in blue and rushing to his apartment came back with an eau de cologne bottle from his grand silver dressing case with the fragrant contents of which he began liberally to sprinkle bonner and blanche <\s>

<s> the ladies from the theatre did not have their treat to greenwich nor did blanche pay her visit to fanny bolton on that day <\s>
<s> and cos who took occasion majestically to inquire of grady what the mischief was and who was crying had for answer that twas a woman another of them and that they were in grady's opinion the cause of most all the mischief in the world <\s>
<s> in which pen begins to doubt about his election whilst pen in his own county was thus carrying on his selfish plans and parliamentary schemes news came to him that lady rockminster had arrived at baymouth and had brought with her our friend laura <\s>
<s> at the announcement that laura his sister was near him pen felt rather guilty <\s>
<s> his wish was to stand higher in her esteem perhaps than in that of any other person in the world <\s>
<s> she was his mother's legacy to him <\s>
<s> he was to be her patron and protector in some sort <\s>
<s> how would she brave the news which he had to tell her and how should he explain the plans which he was meditating <\s>
<s> he felt as if neither he nor blanche could bear laura's dazzling glance of calm scrutiny and as if he would not dare to disclose his worldly hopes and ambitions to that spotless judge <\s>
<s> at her arrival at baymouth he wrote a letter thither which contained a great number of fine phrases and protests of affection and a great deal of easy satire and raillery in the midst of all which mr <\s>
<s> pen could not help feeling that he was in panic and that he was acting like a rogue and hypocrite <\s>
<s> how was it that a simple country girl should be the object of fear and trembling to such an accomplished gentleman as mr <\s>
<s> his worldly tactics and diplomacy his satire and knowledge of the world could not bear the test of her purity he felt somehow <\s>
<s> and he had to own to himself that his affairs were in such a position that he could not tell the truth to that honest soul <\s>
<s> as he rode from clavering to baymouth he felt as guilty as a schoolboy who doesn't know his lesson and is about to face the awful master <\s>
<s> for is not truth the master always and does she not have the power and hold the book <\s>
<s> under the charge of her kind though somewhat wayward and absolute patroness lady rockminster laura had seen somewhat of the world in the last year had gathered some accomplishments and profited by the lessons of society <\s>
<s> many a girl who had been accustomed to that too great tenderness in which laura's early life had been passed would have been unfitted for the changed existence which she now had to lead <\s>
<s> helen worshipped her two children and thought as home bred women will that all the world was made for them or to be considered after them <\s>
<s> she tended laura with a watchfulness of affection which never left her <\s>
<s> if she had a headache the widow was as alarmed as if there had never been an aching head before in the world <\s>
<s> she slept and woke read and moved under her mother's fond superintendence which was now withdrawn from her along with the tender creature whose anxious heart would beat no more <\s>
<s> and painful moments of grief and depression no doubt laura had when she stood in the great careless world alone <\s>
<s> nobody heeded her griefs or her solitude <\s>
<s> she was not quite the equal in social rank of the lady whose companion she was or of the friends and relatives of the imperious but kind old dowager <\s>
<s> some very likely bore her no goodwill some perhaps slighted her it might have been that servants were occasionally rude their mistress certainly was often <\s>
<s> laura not seldom found herself in family meetings the confidence and familiarity of which she felt were interrupted by her intrusion and her sensitiveness of course was wounded at the idea that she should give or feel this annoyance <\s>
<s> how many governesses are there in the world thought cheerful laura how many ladies whose necessities make them slaves and companions by profession <\s>
<s> what bad tempers and coarse unkindness have not these to encounter <\s>
<s> how infinitely better my lot is with these really kind and affectionate people than that of thousands of unprotected girls <\s>
<s> it was with this cordial spirit that our young lady adapted herself to her new position and went in advance of her fortune with a trustful smile <\s>
<s> did you ever know a person who met fortune in that way whom the goddess did not regard kindly <\s>
<s> are not even bad people won by a constant cheerfulness and a pure and affectionate heart <\s>
<s> when the babes in the wood in the ballad looked up fondly and trustfully at those notorious rogues whom their uncle had set to make away with the little folks we all know how one of the rascals relented and made away with the other not having the heart to be unkind to so much innocence and beauty <\s>
<s> oh happy they who have that virgin loving trust and sweet smiling confidence in the world and fear no evil because they think none <\s>
<s> miss laura bell was one of these fortunate persons and besides the gentle widow's little cross which as we have seen pen gave her had such a sparkling and brilliant kohinoor in her bosom as is even more precious than that famous jewel for it not only fetches a price and is retained by its owner in another world where diamonds are stated to be of no value but here too is of inestimable worth to its possessor is a talisman against evil and lightens up the darkness of life like cogia hassan's famous stone <\s>
<s> so that before miss bell had been a year in lady rockminster's house there was not a single person in it whose love she had not won by the use of this talisman <\s>
<s> from the old lady to the lowest dependent of her bounty laura had secured the goodwill and kindness of everybody <\s>
<s> with a mistress of such a temper my lady's woman who had endured her mistress for forty years and had been clawed and scolded and jibed every day and night in that space of time could not be expected to have a good temper of her own and was at first angry against miss laura as she had been against her ladyship's fifteen preceding companions <\s>
<s> but when laura was ill at paris this old woman nursed her in spite of her mistress who was afraid of catching the fever and absolutely fought for her medicine with martha from fairoaks now advanced to be miss laura's own maid <\s>
<s> as she was recovering grandjean the chef wanted to kill her by the numbers of delicacies which he dressed for her and wept when she ate her first slice of chicken <\s>
<s> the swiss major domo of the house celebrated miss bell's praises in almost every european language which he spoke with indifferent incorrectness the coachman was happy to drive her out the page cried when he heard she was ill and calverley and coldstream those two footmen so large so calm ordinarily and so difficult to move broke out into extraordinary hilarity at the news of her convalescence and intoxicated the page at a wine shop to fete laura's recovery <\s>

<s> in which pen begins to doubt about his election whilst pen in his own county was thus carrying on his selfish plans and parliamentary schemes news came to him that lady rockminster had arrived at baymouth and had brought with her our friend laura <\s>
<s> at the announcement that laura his sister was near him pen felt rather guilty <\s>
<s> his wish was to stand higher in her esteem perhaps than in that of any other person in the world <\s>
<s> she was his mother's legacy to him <\s>
<s> he was to be her patron and protector in some sort <\s>
<s> how would she brave the news which he had to tell her and how should he explain the plans which he was meditating <\s>
<s> he felt as if neither he nor blanche could bear laura's dazzling glance of calm scrutiny and as if he would not dare to disclose his worldly hopes and ambitions to that spotless judge <\s>
<s> at her arrival at baymouth he wrote a letter thither which contained a great number of fine phrases and protests of affection and a great deal of easy satire and raillery in the midst of all which mr <\s>
<s> pen could not help feeling that he was in panic and that he was acting like a rogue and hypocrite <\s>
<s> how was it that a simple country girl should be the object of fear and trembling to such an accomplished gentleman as mr <\s>
<s> his worldly tactics and diplomacy his satire and knowledge of the world could not bear the test of her purity he felt somehow <\s>
<s> and he had to own to himself that his affairs were in such a position that he could not tell the truth to that honest soul <\s>
<s> as he rode from clavering to baymouth he felt as guilty as a schoolboy who doesn't know his lesson and is about to face the awful master <\s>
<s> for is not truth the master always and does she not have the power and hold the book <\s>
<s> under the charge of her kind though somewhat wayward and absolute patroness lady rockminster laura had seen somewhat of the world in the last year had gathered some accomplishments and profited by the lessons of society <\s>
<s> many a girl who had been accustomed to that too great tenderness in which laura's early life had been passed would have been unfitted for the changed existence which she now had to lead <\s>
<s> helen worshipped her two children and thought as home bred women will that all the world was made for them or to be considered after them <\s>
<s> she tended laura with a watchfulness of affection which never left her <\s>
<s> if she had a headache the widow was as alarmed as if there had never been an aching head before in the world <\s>
<s> she slept and woke read and moved under her mother's fond superintendence which was now withdrawn from her along with the tender creature whose anxious heart would beat no more <\s>
<s> and painful moments of grief and depression no doubt laura had when she stood in the great careless world alone <\s>
<s> nobody heeded her griefs or her solitude <\s>
<s> she was not quite the equal in social rank of the lady whose companion she was or of the friends and relatives of the imperious but kind old dowager <\s>
<s> some very likely bore her no goodwill some perhaps slighted her it might have been that servants were occasionally rude their mistress certainly was often <\s>
<s> laura not seldom found herself in family meetings the confidence and familiarity of which she felt were interrupted by her intrusion and her sensitiveness of course was wounded at the idea that she should give or feel this annoyance <\s>
<s> how many governesses are there in the world thought cheerful laura how many ladies whose necessities make them slaves and companions by profession <\s>
<s> what bad tempers and coarse unkindness have not these to encounter <\s>
<s> how infinitely better my lot is with these really kind and affectionate people than that of thousands of unprotected girls <\s>

<s> did you ever know a person who met fortune in that way whom the goddess did not regard kindly <\s>
<s> are not even bad people won by a constant cheerfulness and a pure and affectionate heart <\s>
<s> when the babes in the wood in the ballad looked up fondly and trustfully at those notorious rogues whom their uncle had set to make away with the little folks we all know how one of the rascals relented and made away with the other not having the heart to be unkind to so much innocence and beauty <\s>
<s> oh happy they who have that virgin loving trust and sweet smiling confidence in the world and fear no evil because they think none <\s>
<s> miss laura bell was one of these fortunate persons and besides the gentle widow's little cross which as we have seen pen gave her had such a sparkling and brilliant kohinoor in her bosom as is even more precious than that famous jewel for it not only fetches a price and is retained by its owner in another world where diamonds are stated to be of no value but here too is of inestimable worth to its possessor is a talisman against evil and lightens up the darkness of life like cogia hassan's famous stone <\s>
<s> so that before miss bell had been a year in lady rockminster's house there was not a single person in it whose love she had not won by the use of this talisman <\s>
<s> from the old lady to the lowest dependent of her bounty laura had secured the goodwill and kindness of everybody <\s>
<s> with a mistress of such a temper my lady's woman who had endured her mistress for forty years and had been clawed and scolded and jibed every day and night in that space of time could not be expected to have a good temper of her own and was at first angry against miss laura as she had been against her ladyship's fifteen preceding companions <\s>
<s> but when laura was ill at paris this old woman nursed her in spite of her mistress who was afraid of catching the fever and absolutely fought for her medicine with martha from fairoaks now advanced to be miss laura's own maid <\s>
<s> as she was recovering grandjean the chef wanted to kill her by the numbers of delicacies which he dressed for her and wept when she ate her first slice of chicken <\s>
<s> the swiss major domo of the house celebrated miss bell's praises in almost every european language which he spoke with indifferent incorrectness the coachman was happy to drive her out the page cried when he heard she was ill and calverley and coldstream those two footmen so large so calm ordinarily and so difficult to move broke out into extraordinary hilarity at the news of her convalescence and intoxicated the page at a wine shop to fete laura's recovery <\s>

<s> pynsent had married by this time lady diana who had had a considerable dislike to laura for some time was so enthusiastic as to say that she thought miss bell was a very agreeable person and that grandmamma had found a great trouvaille in her <\s>
<s> all this goodwill and kindness laura had acquired not by any arts not by any flattery but by the simple force of good nature and by the blessed gift of pleasing and being pleased <\s>

<s> miss laura bell was one of these fortunate persons and besides the gentle widow's little cross which as we have seen pen gave her had such a sparkling and brilliant kohinoor in her bosom as is even more precious than that famous jewel for it not only fetches a price and is retained by its owner in another world where diamonds are stated to be of no value but here too is of inestimable worth to its possessor is a talisman against evil and lightens up the darkness of life like cogia hassan's famous stone <\s>
<s> so that before miss bell had been a year in lady rockminster's house there was not a single person in it whose love she had not won by the use of this talisman <\s>
<s> from the old lady to the lowest dependent of her bounty laura had secured the goodwill and kindness of everybody <\s>
<s> with a mistress of such a temper my lady's woman who had endured her mistress for forty years and had been clawed and scolded and jibed every day and night in that space of time could not be expected to have a good temper of her own and was at first angry against miss laura as she had been against her ladyship's fifteen preceding companions <\s>
<s> but when laura was ill at paris this old woman nursed her in spite of her mistress who was afraid of catching the fever and absolutely fought for her medicine with martha from fairoaks now advanced to be miss laura's own maid <\s>
<s> as she was recovering grandjean the chef wanted to kill her by the numbers of delicacies which he dressed for her and wept when she ate her first slice of chicken <\s>
<s> the swiss major domo of the house celebrated miss bell's praises in almost every european language which he spoke with indifferent incorrectness the coachman was happy to drive her out the page cried when he heard she was ill and calverley and coldstream those two footmen so large so calm ordinarily and so difficult to move broke out into extraordinary hilarity at the news of her convalescence and intoxicated the page at a wine shop to fete laura's recovery <\s>
<s> even lady diana pynsent our former acquaintance mr <\s>
<s> pynsent had married by this time lady diana who had had a considerable dislike to laura for some time was so enthusiastic as to say that she thought miss bell was a very agreeable person and that grandmamma had found a great trouvaille in her <\s>
<s> all this goodwill and kindness laura had acquired not by any arts not by any flattery but by the simple force of good nature and by the blessed gift of pleasing and being pleased <\s>
<s> on the one or two occasions when he had seen lady rockminster the old lady who did not admire him had been very pitiless and abrupt with our young friend and perhaps pen expected when he came to baymouth to find laura installed in her house in the quality of humble companion and treated no better than himself <\s>
<s> when she heard of his arrival she came running downstairs and i am not sure that she did not embrace him in the presence of calverley and coldstream not that those gentlemen ever told if the fractus orbis had come to a smash if laura instead of kissing pen had taken her scissors and snipped off his head calverley and coldstream would have looked on impavidly without allowing a grain of powder to be disturbed by the calamity <\s>
<s> laura had so much improved in health and looks that pen could not but admire her <\s>
<s> the frank and kind eyes which met his beamed with good health the cheek which he kissed blushed with beauty <\s>
<s> as he looked at her artless and graceful pure and candid he thought he had never seen her so beautiful <\s>
<s> why should he remark her beauty now so much and remark too to himself that he had not remarked it sooner <\s>
<s> he took her fair trustful hand and kissed it fondly he looked in her bright clear eyes and read in them that kindling welcome which he was always sure to find there <\s>
<s> he was affected and touched by the tender tone and the pure sparkling glance their innocence smote him somehow and moved him <\s>
<s> how good you are to me laura sister <\s>
<s> said pen i don't deserve that you should that you should be so kind to me <\s>

<s> betsy or blanche looked quite bewildered and began to scream too once twice thrice and it was her piercing shrieks which captain costigan heard as he walked the court below <\s>
<s> at the sound of these shrieks the perplexed parent clasped his hands his wristbands were open and on one brawny arm you could see letters tattooed in blue and rushing to his apartment came back with an eau de cologne bottle from his grand silver dressing case with the fragrant contents of which he began liberally to sprinkle bonner and blanche <\s>

<s> and cos who took occasion majestically to inquire of grady what the mischief was and who was crying had for answer that twas a woman another of them and that they were in grady's opinion the cause of most all the mischief in the world <\s>
<s> in which pen begins to doubt about his election whilst pen in his own county was thus carrying on his selfish plans and parliamentary schemes news came to him that lady rockminster had arrived at baymouth and had brought with her our friend laura <\s>
<s> at the announcement that laura his sister was near him pen felt rather guilty <\s>
<s> his wish was to stand higher in her esteem perhaps than in that of any other person in the world <\s>
<s> she was his mother's legacy to him <\s>
<s> he was to be her patron and protector in some sort <\s>
<s> how would she brave the news which he had to tell her and how should he explain the plans which he was meditating <\s>
<s> he felt as if neither he nor blanche could bear laura's dazzling glance of calm scrutiny and as if he would not dare to disclose his worldly hopes and ambitions to that spotless judge <\s>
<s> at her arrival at baymouth he wrote a letter thither which contained a great number of fine phrases and protests of affection and a great deal of easy satire and raillery in the midst of all which mr <\s>
<s> pen could not help feeling that he was in panic and that he was acting like a rogue and hypocrite <\s>
<s> how was it that a simple country girl should be the object of fear and trembling to such an accomplished gentleman as mr <\s>
<s> his worldly tactics and diplomacy his satire and knowledge of the world could not bear the test of her purity he felt somehow <\s>
<s> and he had to own to himself that his affairs were in such a position that he could not tell the truth to that honest soul <\s>
<s> as he rode from clavering to baymouth he felt as guilty as a schoolboy who doesn't know his lesson and is about to face the awful master <\s>
<s> for is not truth the master always and does she not have the power and hold the book <\s>
<s> under the charge of her kind though somewhat wayward and absolute patroness lady rockminster laura had seen somewhat of the world in the last year had gathered some accomplishments and profited by the lessons of society <\s>
<s> many a girl who had been accustomed to that too great tenderness in which laura's early life had been passed would have been unfitted for the changed existence which she now had to lead <\s>

<s> in which pen begins to doubt about his election whilst pen in his own county was thus carrying on his selfish plans and parliamentary schemes news came to him that lady rockminster had arrived at baymouth and had brought with her our friend laura <\s>
<s> at the announcement that laura his sister was near him pen felt rather guilty <\s>
<s> his wish was to stand higher in her esteem perhaps than in that of any other person in the world <\s>
<s> she was his mother's legacy to him <\s>
<s> he was to be her patron and protector in some sort <\s>
<s> how would she brave the news which he had to tell her and how should he explain the plans which he was meditating <\s>
<s> he felt as if neither he nor blanche could bear laura's dazzling glance of calm scrutiny and as if he would not dare to disclose his worldly hopes and ambitions to that spotless judge <\s>
<s> at her arrival at baymouth he wrote a letter thither which contained a great number of fine phrases and protests of affection and a great deal of easy satire and raillery in the midst of all which mr <\s>
<s> pen could not help feeling that he was in panic and that he was acting like a rogue and hypocrite <\s>
<s> how was it that a simple country girl should be the object of fear and trembling to such an accomplished gentleman as mr <\s>
<s> his worldly tactics and diplomacy his satire and knowledge of the world could not bear the test of her purity he felt somehow <\s>
<s> and he had to own to himself that his affairs were in such a position that he could not tell the truth to that honest soul <\s>
<s> as he rode from clavering to baymouth he felt as guilty as a schoolboy who doesn't know his lesson and is about to face the awful master <\s>
<s> for is not truth the master always and does she not have the power and hold the book <\s>
<s> under the charge of her kind though somewhat wayward and absolute patroness lady rockminster laura had seen somewhat of the world in the last year had gathered some accomplishments and profited by the lessons of society <\s>
<s> many a girl who had been accustomed to that too great tenderness in which laura's early life had been passed would have been unfitted for the changed existence which she now had to lead <\s>
<s> helen worshipped her two children and thought as home bred women will that all the world was made for them or to be considered after them <\s>
<s> she tended laura with a watchfulness of affection which never left her <\s>
<s> if she had a headache the widow was as alarmed as if there had never been an aching head before in the world <\s>
<s> she slept and woke read and moved under her mother's fond superintendence which was now withdrawn from her along with the tender creature whose anxious heart would beat no more <\s>
<s> and painful moments of grief and depression no doubt laura had when she stood in the great careless world alone <\s>
<s> nobody heeded her griefs or her solitude <\s>
<s> she was not quite the equal in social rank of the lady whose companion she was or of the friends and relatives of the imperious but kind old dowager <\s>
<s> some very likely bore her no goodwill some perhaps slighted her it might have been that servants were occasionally rude their mistress certainly was often <\s>
<s> laura not seldom found herself in family meetings the confidence and familiarity of which she felt were interrupted by her intrusion and her sensitiveness of course was wounded at the idea that she should give or feel this annoyance <\s>
<s> how many governesses are there in the world thought cheerful laura how many ladies whose necessities make them slaves and companions by profession <\s>
<s> what bad tempers and coarse unkindness have not these to encounter <\s>
<s> how infinitely better my lot is with these really kind and affectionate people than that of thousands of unprotected girls <\s>
<s> it was with this cordial spirit that our young lady adapted herself to her new position and went in advance of her fortune with a trustful smile <\s>
<s> did you ever know a person who met fortune in that way whom the goddess did not regard kindly <\s>
<s> are not even bad people won by a constant cheerfulness and a pure and affectionate heart <\s>
<s> when the babes in the wood in the ballad looked up fondly and trustfully at those notorious rogues whom their uncle had set to make away with the little folks we all know how one of the rascals relented and made away with the other not having the heart to be unkind to so much innocence and beauty <\s>
<s> oh happy they who have that virgin loving trust and sweet smiling confidence in the world and fear no evil because they think none <\s>
<s> miss laura bell was one of these fortunate persons and besides the gentle widow's little cross which as we have seen pen gave her had such a sparkling and brilliant kohinoor in her bosom as is even more precious than that famous jewel for it not only fetches a price and is retained by its owner in another world where diamonds are stated to be of no value but here too is of inestimable worth to its possessor is a talisman against evil and lightens up the darkness of life like cogia hassan's famous stone <\s>
<s> so that before miss bell had been a year in lady rockminster's house there was not a single person in it whose love she had not won by the use of this talisman <\s>
<s> from the old lady to the lowest dependent of her bounty laura had secured the goodwill and kindness of everybody <\s>
<s> with a mistress of such a temper my lady's woman who had endured her mistress for forty years and had been clawed and scolded and jibed every day and night in that space of time could not be expected to have a good temper of her own and was at first angry against miss laura as she had been against her ladyship's fifteen preceding companions <\s>
<s> but when laura was ill at paris this old woman nursed her in spite of her mistress who was afraid of catching the fever and absolutely fought for her medicine with martha from fairoaks now advanced to be miss laura's own maid <\s>
<s> as she was recovering grandjean the chef wanted to kill her by the numbers of delicacies which he dressed for her and wept when she ate her first slice of chicken <\s>
<s> the swiss major domo of the house celebrated miss bell's praises in almost every european language which he spoke with indifferent incorrectness the coachman was happy to drive her out the page cried when he heard she was ill and calverley and coldstream those two footmen so large so calm ordinarily and so difficult to move broke out into extraordinary hilarity at the news of her convalescence and intoxicated the page at a wine shop to fete laura's recovery <\s>
<s> even lady diana pynsent our former acquaintance mr <\s>
<s> pynsent had married by this time lady diana who had had a considerable dislike to laura for some time was so enthusiastic as to say that she thought miss bell was a very agreeable person and that grandmamma had found a great trouvaille in her <\s>
<s> all this goodwill and kindness laura had acquired not by any arts not by any flattery but by the simple force of good nature and by the blessed gift of pleasing and being pleased <\s>

<s> as he rode from clavering to baymouth he felt as guilty as a schoolboy who doesn't know his lesson and is about to face the awful master <\s>
<s> for is not truth the master always and does she not have the power and hold the book <\s>
<s> under the charge of her kind though somewhat wayward and absolute patroness lady rockminster laura had seen somewhat of the world in the last year had gathered some accomplishments and profited by the lessons of society <\s>
<s> many a girl who had been accustomed to that too great tenderness in which laura's early life had been passed would have been unfitted for the changed existence which she now had to lead <\s>
<s> helen worshipped her two children and thought as home bred women will that all the world was made for them or to be considered after them <\s>
<s> she tended laura with a watchfulness of affection which never left her <\s>
<s> if she had a headache the widow was as alarmed as if there had never been an aching head before in the world <\s>
<s> she slept and woke read and moved under her mother's fond superintendence which was now withdrawn from her along with the tender creature whose anxious heart would beat no more <\s>
<s> and painful moments of grief and depression no doubt laura had when she stood in the great careless world alone <\s>
<s> nobody heeded her griefs or her solitude <\s>
<s> she was not quite the equal in social rank of the lady whose companion she was or of the friends and relatives of the imperious but kind old dowager <\s>
<s> some very likely bore her no goodwill some perhaps slighted her it might have been that servants were occasionally rude their mistress certainly was often <\s>
<s> laura not seldom found herself in family meetings the confidence and familiarity of which she felt were interrupted by her intrusion and her sensitiveness of course was wounded at the idea that she should give or feel this annoyance <\s>
<s> how many governesses are there in the world thought cheerful laura how many ladies whose necessities make them slaves and companions by profession <\s>
<s> what bad tempers and coarse unkindness have not these to encounter <\s>
<s> how infinitely better my lot is with these really kind and affectionate people than that of thousands of unprotected girls <\s>
<s> it was with this cordial spirit that our young lady adapted herself to her new position and went in advance of her fortune with a trustful smile <\s>
<s> did you ever know a person who met fortune in that way whom the goddess did not regard kindly <\s>
<s> are not even bad people won by a constant cheerfulness and a pure and affectionate heart <\s>
<s> when the babes in the wood in the ballad looked up fondly and trustfully at those notorious rogues whom their uncle had set to make away with the little folks we all know how one of the rascals relented and made away with the other not having the heart to be unkind to so much innocence and beauty <\s>
<s> oh happy they who have that virgin loving trust and sweet smiling confidence in the world and fear no evil because they think none <\s>
<s> miss laura bell was one of these fortunate persons and besides the gentle widow's little cross which as we have seen pen gave her had such a sparkling and brilliant kohinoor in her bosom as is even more precious than that famous jewel for it not only fetches a price and is retained by its owner in another world where diamonds are stated to be of no value but here too is of inestimable worth to its possessor is a talisman against evil and lightens up the darkness of life like cogia hassan's famous stone <\s>
<s> so that before miss bell had been a year in lady rockminster's house there was not a single person in it whose love she had not won by the use of this talisman <\s>
<s> from the old lady to the lowest dependent of her bounty laura had secured the goodwill and kindness of everybody <\s>
<s> with a mistress of such a temper my lady's woman who had endured her mistress for forty years and had been clawed and scolded and jibed every day and night in that space of time could not be expected to have a good temper of her own and was at first angry against miss laura as she had been against her ladyship's fifteen preceding companions <\s>
<s> but when laura was ill at paris this old woman nursed her in spite of her mistress who was afraid of catching the fever and absolutely fought for her medicine with martha from fairoaks now advanced to be miss laura's own maid <\s>
<s> as she was recovering grandjean the chef wanted to kill her by the numbers of delicacies which he dressed for her and wept when she ate her first slice of chicken <\s>
<s> the swiss major domo of the house celebrated miss bell's praises in almost every european language which he spoke with indifferent incorrectness the coachman was happy to drive her out the page cried when he heard she was ill and calverley and coldstream those two footmen so large so calm ordinarily and so difficult to move broke out into extraordinary hilarity at the news of her convalescence and intoxicated the page at a wine shop to fete laura's recovery <\s>
<s> even lady diana pynsent our former acquaintance mr <\s>
<s> pynsent had married by this time lady diana who had had a considerable dislike to laura for some time was so enthusiastic as to say that she thought miss bell was a very agreeable person and that grandmamma had found a great trouvaille in her <\s>
<s> all this goodwill and kindness laura had acquired not by any arts not by any flattery but by the simple force of good nature and by the blessed gift of pleasing and being pleased <\s>
<s> on the one or two occasions when he had seen lady rockminster the old lady who did not admire him had been very pitiless and abrupt with our young friend and perhaps pen expected when he came to baymouth to find laura installed in her house in the quality of humble companion and treated no better than himself <\s>
<s> when she heard of his arrival she came running downstairs and i am not sure that she did not embrace him in the presence of calverley and coldstream not that those gentlemen ever told if the fractus orbis had come to a smash if laura instead of kissing pen had taken her scissors and snipped off his head calverley and coldstream would have looked on impavidly without allowing a grain of powder to be disturbed by the calamity <\s>
<s> laura had so much improved in health and looks that pen could not but admire her <\s>
<s> the frank and kind eyes which met his beamed with good health the cheek which he kissed blushed with beauty <\s>
<s> as he looked at her artless and graceful pure and candid he thought he had never seen her so beautiful <\s>
<s> why should he remark her beauty now so much and remark too to himself that he had not remarked it sooner <\s>
<s> he took her fair trustful hand and kissed it fondly he looked in her bright clear eyes and read in them that kindling welcome which he was always sure to find there <\s>
<s> he was affected and touched by the tender tone and the pure sparkling glance their innocence smote him somehow and moved him <\s>
<s> how good you are to me laura sister <\s>
<s> said pen i don't deserve that you should that you should be so kind to me <\s>

<s> on the one or two occasions when he had seen lady rockminster the old lady who did not admire him had been very pitiless and abrupt with our young friend and perhaps pen expected when he came to baymouth to find laura installed in her house in the quality of humble companion and treated no better than himself <\s>
<s> when she heard of his arrival she came running downstairs and i am not sure that she did not embrace him in the presence of calverley and coldstream not that those gentlemen ever told if the fractus orbis had come to a smash if laura instead of kissing pen had taken her scissors and snipped off his head calverley and coldstream would have looked on impavidly without allowing a grain of powder to be disturbed by the calamity <\s>
<s> laura had so much improved in health and looks that pen could not but admire her <\s>
<s> the frank and kind eyes which met his beamed with good health the cheek which he kissed blushed with beauty <\s>
<s> as he looked at her artless and graceful pure and candid he thought he had never seen her so beautiful <\s>
<s> why should he remark her beauty now so much and remark too to himself that he had not remarked it sooner <\s>
<s> he took her fair trustful hand and kissed it fondly he looked in her bright clear eyes and read in them that kindling welcome which he was always sure to find there <\s>
<s> he was affected and touched by the tender tone and the pure sparkling glance their innocence smote him somehow and moved him <\s>

<s> betsy or blanche looked quite bewildered and began to scream too once twice thrice and it was her piercing shrieks which captain costigan heard as he walked the court below <\s>
<s> at the sound of these shrieks the perplexed parent clasped his hands his wristbands were open and on one brawny arm you could see letters tattooed in blue and rushing to his apartment came back with an eau de cologne bottle from his grand silver dressing case with the fragrant contents of which he began liberally to sprinkle bonner and blanche <\s>

<s> and cos who took occasion majestically to inquire of grady what the mischief was and who was crying had for answer that twas a woman another of them and that they were in grady's opinion the cause of most all the mischief in the world <\s>
<s> in which pen begins to doubt about his election whilst pen in his own county was thus carrying on his selfish plans and parliamentary schemes news came to him that lady rockminster had arrived at baymouth and had brought with her our friend laura <\s>
<s> at the announcement that laura his sister was near him pen felt rather guilty <\s>
<s> his wish was to stand higher in her esteem perhaps than in that of any other person in the world <\s>
<s> she was his mother's legacy to him <\s>
<s> he was to be her patron and protector in some sort <\s>
<s> how would she brave the news which he had to tell her and how should he explain the plans which he was meditating <\s>
<s> he felt as if neither he nor blanche could bear laura's dazzling glance of calm scrutiny and as if he would not dare to disclose his worldly hopes and ambitions to that spotless judge <\s>
<s> at her arrival at baymouth he wrote a letter thither which contained a great number of fine phrases and protests of affection and a great deal of easy satire and raillery in the midst of all which mr <\s>
<s> pen could not help feeling that he was in panic and that he was acting like a rogue and hypocrite <\s>
<s> how was it that a simple country girl should be the object of fear and trembling to such an accomplished gentleman as mr <\s>
<s> his worldly tactics and diplomacy his satire and knowledge of the world could not bear the test of her purity he felt somehow <\s>
<s> and he had to own to himself that his affairs were in such a position that he could not tell the truth to that honest soul <\s>
<s> as he rode from clavering to baymouth he felt as guilty as a schoolboy who doesn't know his lesson and is about to face the awful master <\s>
<s> for is not truth the master always and does she not have the power and hold the book <\s>
<s> under the charge of her kind though somewhat wayward and absolute patroness lady rockminster laura had seen somewhat of the world in the last year had gathered some accomplishments and profited by the lessons of society <\s>
<s> many a girl who had been accustomed to that too great tenderness in which laura's early life had been passed would have been unfitted for the changed existence which she now had to lead <\s>
<s> helen worshipped her two children and thought as home bred women will that all the world was made for them or to be considered after them <\s>
<s> she tended laura with a watchfulness of affection which never left her <\s>
<s> if she had a headache the widow was as alarmed as if there had never been an aching head before in the world <\s>
<s> she slept and woke read and moved under her mother's fond superintendence which was now withdrawn from her along with the tender creature whose anxious heart would beat no more <\s>
<s> and painful moments of grief and depression no doubt laura had when she stood in the great careless world alone <\s>
<s> nobody heeded her griefs or her solitude <\s>
<s> she was not quite the equal in social rank of the lady whose companion she was or of the friends and relatives of the imperious but kind old dowager <\s>
<s> some very likely bore her no goodwill some perhaps slighted her it might have been that servants were occasionally rude their mistress certainly was often <\s>
<s> laura not seldom found herself in family meetings the confidence and familiarity of which she felt were interrupted by her intrusion and her sensitiveness of course was wounded at the idea that she should give or feel this annoyance <\s>
<s> how many governesses are there in the world thought cheerful laura how many ladies whose necessities make them slaves and companions by profession <\s>
<s> what bad tempers and coarse unkindness have not these to encounter <\s>
<s> how infinitely better my lot is with these really kind and affectionate people than that of thousands of unprotected girls <\s>

<s> did you ever know a person who met fortune in that way whom the goddess did not regard kindly <\s>
<s> are not even bad people won by a constant cheerfulness and a pure and affectionate heart <\s>

<s> oh happy they who have that virgin loving trust and sweet smiling confidence in the world and fear no evil because they think none <\s>
<s> miss laura bell was one of these fortunate persons and besides the gentle widow's little cross which as we have seen pen gave her had such a sparkling and brilliant kohinoor in her bosom as is even more precious than that famous jewel for it not only fetches a price and is retained by its owner in another world where diamonds are stated to be of no value but here too is of inestimable worth to its possessor is a talisman against evil and lightens up the darkness of life like cogia hassan's famous stone <\s>
<s> so that before miss bell had been a year in lady rockminster's house there was not a single person in it whose love she had not won by the use of this talisman <\s>
